[D] TEXTILES -- The CPC class D groups inventions related to textiles, encompassing the preparation of fibers, yarns and filaments, methods for weaving, knitting, crocheting or bonding fabrics, and processes for finishing, dyeing, printing or otherwise treating textile articles. It also covers textile testing, repair techniques and the manufacture of textile-reinforced composites.
[D01] TEXTILES OR FLEXIBLE MATERIALS NOT OTHERWISE PROVIDED FOR -- In this class, the following terms are used with the meanings indicated: "fibre" means a relatively-short, elongated member of natural or man-made material; "filament" means an endless or quasi-endless, elongated member of natural or man-made material; "yarn" means a unitary assembly of fibres, usually produced by spinning; "thread" means an assembly of yarns or filaments, usually produced by twisting; "synthetic" fibres or filaments means fibres or filaments or the like manufactured from synthesising polymers or small molecules. Examples are polyamide, acrylic, polyester or carbon fibres; "artificial" fibres or filaments means fibres or filaments or the like manufactured by man from natural polymers or their derivatives. Examples are regenerated cellulosic fibres or semi-synthetic fibres; "man-made" fibres or filaments means fibres or filaments which are manufactured by man including "synthetic" or "artificial" fibres.
[D01B] MECHANICAL TREATMENT OF NATURAL FIBROUS OR FILAMENTARY MATERIAL TO OBTAIN FIBRES OF FILAMENTS, e.g. FOR SPINNING -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The extraction of staple fibres, i.e. fibres of limited length, from natural materials like the seeds, leaves or stalks of plants or from silk.  **Glossary:** - Fibre: a relatively-short, elongated member of natural or artificial material - Filament: an endless or quasi-endless, elongated member of natural (e.g. silk) or artificial material - Yarn: a unitary assembly of fibres, usually produced by spinning - Thread: an assembly of yarns or filaments, usually produced by twisting
[D01B 1/00] Mechanical separation of fibres from plant material, e.g. seeds, leaves, stalks -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The process steps used in separating fibres from the seeds (mainly cotton) and stalks or leaves (mainly flax or hemp) of plant material.  **Glossary:** - Stalk: the main stem of a herbaceous plant.
[D01B 1/02] Separating vegetable fibres from seeds, e.g. cotton -- The CPC entry D01B 1/02 covers mechanical methods for separating vegetable fibres from seeds, such as extracting cotton fibres from the seed coat. It applies to treatments that detach natural fibrous material from plant parts like seeds, leaves or stalks to produce filamentary fibres for further processing.
[D01B 1/04] Ginning -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The initial separation of harvested fibres and seeds in so called ginning machines.  **Glossary:** - Ginning: the process of separating cotton fibres from their seeds and other agricultural waste
[D01B 1/06] Roller gins, e.g. Macarthy type -- Roller gins of the Macarthy type are machines that mechanically separate fibres from plant material such as seeds, leaves or stalks to produce raw filamentary fibres for spinning. They belong to the CPC subclass D01B 1/06 covering mechanical treatment of natural fibrous or filamentary materials in the textiles sector.
[D01B 1/08] Saw gins -- Saw gins are mechanical devices that separate fibers from plant material such as seeds, leaves or stalks by cutting the material with a saw-like action, producing loose fibers suitable for spinning. They belong to the CPC group D01B 1/08 dealing with mechanical treatment of natural fibrous or filamentary material.
[D01B 1/10] Separating vegetable fibres from stalks or leaves -- D01B 1/10 relates to mechanical methods for extracting vegetable fibres from plant stalks or leaves, such as flax or hemp, producing raw fibre suitable for subsequent textile processes like spinning.
[D01B 1/12] Rippling -- **Definition:** This place covers:  An early stage process of pulling the dry flax plants through coarse combs for removing the seeds from the stalks.  **Glossary:** - Rippling: the process of removing the seeds from the flax stalks
[D01B 1/14] Breaking or scutching, e.g. of flax -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The mechanical separation of fibres from the wood of the stalks.  **Glossary:** - Scutching: the process whereby the woody portion of the stalks is removed by crushing them between two metal rolls
[D01B 1/16] with devices dependent on a bending action to break or loosen fibre-bearing materials -- The CPC subclass D01B 1/16 covers mechanical processes that separate natural fibres from plant material by using devices that act through a bending motion to break or loosen the fibre-bearing parts, such as seeds, leaves or stalks, in preparation for spinning. This is a specific method of mechanical treatment within textile processing.
[D01B 1/18] with stamping devices -- This subclass covers processes that mechanically separate natural fibers from plant parts such as seeds, leaves or stalks using stamping devices. The stamping action helps to loosen and detach the fibers for subsequent spinning or further treatment. It falls under the broader category of mechanical treatment of natural fibrous or filamentary material in textile manufacturing.
[D01B 1/20] with scraping devices -- This subclass covers processes that mechanically separate natural fibers from plant material-such as seeds, leaves or stalks-by using scraping devices like blades or scrapers to detach the fibers before further textile processing. It is part of the mechanical treatment of natural fibrous or filamentary material for fiber production.
[D01B 1/22] with crushing or breaking rollers or plates -- This subclass covers the mechanical extraction of natural fibres from plant sources such as seeds, leaves or stalks by means of crushing or breaking rollers or plates. It is used in the preparation of raw fibres for spinning in textile manufacturing.
[D01B 1/24] with toothed or other pointed devices -- This subclass covers mechanical processes for extracting individual fibres from plant material such as seeds, leaves or stalks by means of toothed or other pointed tools. The devices may be comb-like, serrated knives, needles or similar implements that tear, scrape or pull the fibres away from the bulk material, facilitating subsequent spinning or other textile treatments.
[D01B 1/26] with beaters rotating about an axis parallel with the fibre bundle -- The classification covers a mechanical process in which beaters rotate about an axis parallel to the fibre bundle to separate individual fibres from plant sources such as seeds, leaves or stalks, preparing them for further steps like spinning. It falls under the broader category of mechanical separation of natural fibrous material.
[D01B 1/28] with beaters rotating about an axis perpendicular to the fibre bundle -- D01B 1/28 covers mechanical separation of natural fibres in which beaters rotate about an axis that is perpendicular to the fibre bundle, such as in equipment that extracts fibres from seeds, leaves or stalks for subsequent spinning. The arrangement provides a cutting or crushing action that loosens and isolates individual filaments.
[D01B 1/30] Details of machines -- The CPC subclass D01B 1/30 covers machines and related arrangements that mechanically separate natural plant fibres-from seeds, leaves or stalks-to produce filamentary fibres for spinning. It includes details of equipment such as decorticators, hammer mills, shredders and other devices used in the extraction and initial processing of these fibres.
[D01B 1/32] Feeding arrangements -- Feeding arrangements refers to the devices and methods that deliver plant material such as seeds, leaves or stalks into machines that mechanically separate fibres. It includes hoppers, conveyors, feeding rollers and other mechanisms that position and supply the material for fibre extraction. This entry is part of the subclass dealing with mechanical treatment of natural fibres for spinning.
[D01B 1/34] Devices holding fibres or fibre-bearing materials during treatment -- This subclass concerns apparatus that securely hold or support natural fibres, fibre bundles or fibre-bearing raw material while they undergo mechanical processing such as separation, cleaning or opening. The devices may include clamps, trays, holders, conveyors or frames designed to keep the material in place during treatment. Used in textile manufacturing for extracting fibres from plant sources.
[D01B 1/36] Conveying devices, e.g. moving bands or ropes -- The code D01B 1/36 covers conveying devices used in the mechanical processing of natural fibres, such as moving belts, ropes or other transport mechanisms that move plant material during fibre extraction. These devices assist in separating fibres from seeds, leaves or stalks.
[D01B 1/38] Delivery or discharge arrangements -- The code D01B 1/38 covers the means for delivering or discharging fibers produced during the mechanical separation of plant material. It includes arrangements such as conveyors, blow-pipes, nozzles and other devices that transport, guide, or release the extracted filaments for further processing such as spinning.
[D01B 1/40] Arrangements for disposing of non-fibrous materials -- The D01B 1/40 entry covers equipment and methods used to remove or handle non-fibrous residues-such as seeds, leaves or stalk fragments-generated during the mechanical separation of plant-derived fibres. It describes arrangements for collecting, transporting or discarding these unwanted materials within textile fibre-production processes.
[D01B 1/42] employing liquids -- D01B 1/42 covers processes that separate natural fibers from plant parts such as seeds, leaves or stalks by applying liquids, often as part of mechanical treatment to prepare fibers for spinning.
[D01B 1/44] Framework -- D01B 1/44 covers the mechanical separation of natural fibers from plant material such as seeds, leaves or stalks, using a framework of combs, rollers, belts or similar structures to detach and collect the filaments for subsequent spinning. It is a sub-category of treatments that produce fibers from raw botanical sources.
[D01B 1/46] Driving arrangements -- Driving arrangements cover the power-source and transmission systems that operate machines for mechanically separating natural fibers from plant material. This includes motors, gear trains, belts, clutches and other mechanisms that drive the rollers, hammers or other devices used in fiber extraction for spinning.
[D01B 1/48] Drying retted fibres -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Only the drying methods and apparatuses of fibres obtained from retting.  **Glossary:** - Retting: a process employing the action of bacteria and moisture on stalks (e.g. flax stalks) to dissolve or rot away much of the cellular tissues and gummy substances (i.e. pectin) surrounding bast-fibre bundles (i.e. fibre loosening). Basic methods include natural retting (i.e. dew retting or water retting) or chemical retting.
[D01B 1/50] Obtaining fibres from other specified vegetable matter, e.g. peat, Spanish moss -- This CPC subclass covers processes for mechanically extracting fibers from unconventional vegetable sources such as peat or Spanish moss. It falls under the textile group dealing with mechanical treatment of natural fibrous or filamentary material to produce fibers for spinning, involving actions like crushing, grinding or combing.
[D01B 3/00] Mechanical removal of impurities from animal fibres -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The mechanical cleaning of wools (e.g. scouring and cleaning stages to remove organic, vegetal and mineral matters).
[D01B 3/02] De-burring machines or apparatus -- De-burring machines or apparatus are equipment designed to mechanically remove burrs, scales, and other surface impurities from natural fibrous or filamentary materials such as animal fibres, preparing them for further processing like spinning. The devices typically use cutting, brushing, or friction actions to clean the fibres without damaging their structural integrity. This subclass falls under the treatment of textiles to obtain clean filaments for subsequent use.
[D01B 3/025] Removing pieces of metal -- The subclass covers mechanical processes that extract metal contaminants such as wire fragments or fasteners from natural fibre material during preparation for spinning, using actions like combing, carding or other separation techniques to remove the metal pieces from the fibre mass.
[D01B 3/04] Machines or apparatus for washing or scouring loose wool fibres -- The CPC subclass D01B 3/04 covers machines and apparatus designed to wash or scour loose wool fibres, removing dirt, grease and other impurities before spinning. It is part of the broader mechanical treatment category for natural fibrous or filamentary materials, focusing on the cleaning stage of wool processing.
[D01B 3/06] with circular movement of either wool or liquid -- This subclass covers mechanical treatment of natural fibrous or filamentary material in which a circular motion is applied to the wool or to a liquid medium that contacts the fibres, facilitating impurity removal, opening or loosening of the fibres during processing.
[D01B 3/08] with longitudinal movement of either wool or liquid -- D01B 3/08 covers mechanical cleaning of animal fibres where the wool or a liquid moves longitudinally along the material, typically to remove impurities such as grease, dirt, or vegetable matter during processes like scouring or carding. This method is used to prepare fibres for spinning by ensuring uniform tension and thorough removal of contaminants.
[D01B 3/10] Details of machines or apparatus -- D01B 3/10 covers the design and components of machines used to mechanically remove impurities from animal fibres such as wool, as part of processes that prepare natural fibres for spinning. It includes apparatus features, drive arrangements and cleaning mechanisms that separate foreign matter while preserving fibre integrity.
[D01B 5/00] Hackling or heckling machines -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The combing out of flax or hemp fibres by hackling devices, that perform a discontinuous linear combing movement (i.e. by combs that get finer and finer) to separate stalk remains from the fibres.
[D01B 5/02] Details
[D01B 5/04] Apparatus for feeding, holding, or conveying materials to or in machines -- D01B 5/04 covers devices that move, position, or retain textile or flexible material during processing, especially in hackling or heckling machines for preparing natural fibers for spinning. The apparatus includes feeders, chutes, conveyors, clamps and similar mechanisms that deliver the material to the treatment zone or transport it within the machine.
[D01B 5/06] Construction, mounting, or operating features of heckling devices -- D01B 5/06 covers the structural and functional aspects of heckling or hackling machines used to straighten and separate natural fibres during mechanical treatment for spinning. The classification includes design elements, mounting arrangements, and operating mechanisms that enable the comb-like process of pulling fibres through plates or wires.
[D01B 5/08] Arrangements for removing, or disposing of, tow or waste -- This CPC subclass D01B 5/08 covers the layout and mechanisms in hackling or heckling equipment that separate and discard tow, short fibres, or other waste generated during the mechanical preparation of natural fibres for spinning. The focus is on devices that convey, collect, or eliminate the waste stream to keep the main fibre flow clean and efficient.
[D01B 5/10] Touch pins or other ending devices -- Touch pins or other ending devices are components attached to hackling or heckling machines that engage the fiber bundle as it exits the treatment zone, guiding and securing the strands for subsequent processing such as spinning. They help maintain alignment, control tension, and prevent breakage of the filaments during mechanical treatment of natural fibrous or filamentary material.
[D01B 5/12] Framework -- D01B 5/12 covers machines that perform hackling or heckling, a mechanical treatment that combs and straightens natural fibers to prepare them for spinning. The classification is part of the textiles hierarchy for processing fibrous or filamentary materials, specifically describing the framework of equipment used in this treatment.
[D01B 5/14] Driving arrangements -- The D01B 5/14 subclass concerns the drive or power-transmission systems that propel hackling or heckling machines used in the mechanical treatment of natural fibrous or filamentary textiles, providing the motion needed to comb, straighten and separate fibers for subsequent spinning.
[D01B 5/16] Arrangements for confining or removing dust or the like -- The subclass D01B 5/16 concerns any arrangement that confines or removes dust produced during hackling or heckling of natural fibres. It includes hoods, ducts, filters, suction ports and related collection systems that keep the work area clean and protect operators and equipment.
[D01B 7/00] Obtaining silk fibres or filaments -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The extraction of silk filaments from silkworm cocoons, and their conversion into staple fibres.
[D01B 7/02] Cleaning or classifying silk cocoons -- The D01B 7/02 sub-group relates to methods for cleaning or sorting silk cocoons before the silk filaments are extracted. It includes operations such as removal of foreign matter, debris or damaged cocoons and classification of cocoons by size or quality to prepare them for subsequent reeling or degumming.
[D01B 7/04] Reeling silk -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The unwinding of silk cocoons to gain the silk filament.
[D01B 7/06] Obtaining silk from cocoons or portions thereof not suitable for reeling -- This CPC subclass D01B 7/06 covers processes for extracting silk fibers from whole cocoons or fragments that cannot be directly reeled. It includes mechanical or chemical steps to separate and clean the fibroin filaments for subsequent spinning or textile use.
[D01B 9/00] Other mechanical treatment of natural fibrous or filamentary material to obtain fibres or filaments -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Other mechanical treatment of natural fibrous or filamentary material to obtain fibres or filaments (e.g. fibre content determination, colour alteration at fibre processing level).
[D01C] CHEMICAL OR BIOLOGICAL TREATMENT OF NATURAL FILAMENTARY OR FIBROUS MATERIAL TO OBTAIN FILAMENTS OR FIBRES FOR SPINNING -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Chemical or biological treatment of natural filamentary or fibrous materials to obtain filaments or fibres that are subsequently used for spinning, i.e. the recovery of the fibres and/or filaments from natural materials. It also covers the carbonisation of rags and other fibrous materials to recover animal fibres. Please note that in this context "carbonisation" does not mean that carbon fibres are produced, but only that vegetable impurities are removed from the fibres, usually by an aqueous acidic treatment.  **Glossary:** - Fibre: a relatively-short, elongated member of natural or artificial material; - Filament: an endless or quasi-endless, elongated member of natural or artificial material - Yarn: a unitary assembly of fibres, usually produced by spinning; - Thread: an assembly of yarns or filaments, usually produced by twisting
[D01C 1/00] Treatment of vegetable material -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The treatment of vegetable materials to obtain fibres, e.g. enzymatic retting in the absence of living organisms
[D01C 1/02] by chemical methods to obtain bast fibres -- D01C 1/02 covers chemical processes used to extract and convert bast fibres from plant stems into usable textile fibres. It includes treatments such as retting, pulping and other chemical methods that break down lignin and hemicellulose to free the cellulose fibres for subsequent spinning.
[D01C 1/04] Bacteriological retting -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Retting in the presence of bacteria or other organisms.
[D01C 3/00] Treatment of animal material, e.g. chemical scouring of wool -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The treatment of animal materials to obtain fibres, e.g. wool scouring, silk degumming.
[D01C 3/02] De-gumming silk -- The D01C 3/02 entry covers the chemical removal of the gummy sericin coating from raw silk, a process known as de-gumming, to yield clean fibroin suitable for spinning into yarn or fabric. It falls under textile treatments that prepare animal-derived fibers for further use.
[D01C 5/00] Carbonising rags to recover animal fibres -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The carbonisation of rags or others fibrous materials to recover animal fibres.
[D01D] MECHANICAL METHODS OR APPARATUS IN THE MANUFACTURE OF ARTIFICIAL FILAMENTS, THREADS, FIBRES, BRISTLES OR RIBBONS -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Mechanical methods and apparatus for the manufacture of artificial fibres and filaments.  It does also cover the physical and mechanical treatment of fibres and filaments during their production, e.g. before winding (after production: D01G , D02 ).  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Working or processing of metal wire -> B21F - Production of metallic filaments -> B22D11/00 , B22F1/06 - Production of glass fibres -> C03B37/00 - Production of ceramic fibres -> C04B35/62227 - Apparatus specially adapted for the manufacture of carbon filaments are classified -> D01F9/00 - Processes starting from pre-made fibres or filaments, such as the production of yarns from single filaments -> D02G , D02J  **Glossary:** - Fibre: a relatively-short, elongated member of natural or artificial material; - Filament: an endless or quasi-endless, elongated member of natural or artificial material; - Thread: an assembly of yarns or filaments, usually produced by twisting. - Yarn: a unitary assembly of fibres, usually produced by spinning;
[D01D 1/00] Treatment of filament-forming or like material -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The treatment of the fibre-forming material before extrusion.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Working of plastics or substances in a plastic state, in general -> B29
[D01D 10/00] Physical treatment of artificial filaments or the like during manufacture, i.e. during a continuous production process before the filaments have been collected -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Physical treatment of the filaments or the like during their manufacture, i.e. during a continuous production process before the filaments have been collected.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Chemical or physicochemical treatment during manufacture -> D01F11/00 - Mechanical treatment after manufacture -> D01G , D02 - Spinning of yarns -> D01H - Yarns -> D02G3/00 - Production of fabrics -> D03 , D04 , D05
[D01D 10/02] Heat treatment -- The D01D 10/02 entry covers heat treatment applied to artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons while they are still being produced in a continuous process, before the material is collected. It falls under mechanical methods for manufacturing these textile products.
[D01D 10/04] Supporting filaments or the like during their treatment -- D01D 10/04 covers apparatus or methods that support artificial filaments, threads or ribbons while they undergo physical treatment such as drawing, heating, stretching or coating during a continuous manufacturing line before the material is collected. The claim includes guides, rollers, tensioning devices or other supports that keep the filaments aligned and under controlled tension during processing.
[D01D 10/0409] on bobbins -- This CPC subclass deals with physical treatment of artificial filaments while they remain on bobbins during a continuous production process, covering actions such as tensioning, heating, or coating applied before the filaments are collected. It belongs to the D01D 10/04 group of mechanical methods for manufacturing textiles and flexible materials.
[D01D 10/0418] as cakes or similar coreless thread packages -- The CPC subgroup D01D 10/0418 deals with physical treatment of artificial filaments during continuous manufacture to produce coreless thread packages, such as cakes or similar forms. It falls under mechanical methods for producing textiles, specifically the processing of artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons before they are collected.
[D01D 10/0427] as hanks -- The CPC subclass D01D 10/0427 falls under mechanical methods for making artificial filaments and covers physical treatment of the filaments during continuous manufacture before they are gathered, specifically when the filaments are formed into hanks. It includes operations such as stretching, crimping, heating or other mechanical actions applied to the filament while it remains in the production line.
[D01D 10/0436] while in continuous movement  forwarding filamentary material  B65H51/00
[D01D 10/0445] using rollers with mutually inclined axes -- The CPC entry D01D 10/0445 covers the use of rollers whose axes are inclined relative to each other to physically treat artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons during continuous production before collection. It belongs to the textile subclass dealing with mechanical methods for manufacturing artificial filament products.
[D01D 10/0454] using reels -- This CPC subclass concerns the use of reels in the physical treatment of artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons during continuous manufacturing, applied before the filaments are collected.
[D01D 10/0463] the filaments being maintained parallel -- The CPC entry D01D 10/0463 covers mechanical steps or devices that keep artificial filaments, threads, fibres or similar material oriented parallel to each other during continuous production, before they are collected. Maintaining this alignment improves uniformity and performance of the finished product.
[D01D 10/0472] the filaments being supported on endless bands -- The subclass pertains to continuous mechanical treatment of artificial filaments in which the filaments are supported on moving endless bands during processes such as drawing, heating or coating before collection. It falls under textile manufacturing methods for synthetic fibres.
[D01D 10/0481] the filaments passing through a tube -- This subclass concerns continuous-process treatments in which artificial filaments are conveyed through a tube or conduit, allowing operations such as heating, cooling, drawing, coating, tensioning or exposure to gases or liquids before the filaments are collected. The tube may be stationary or moving and serves to modify the filament's physical characteristics during manufacture.
[D01D 10/049] as staple fibres -- The D01D 10/049 subclass covers physical treatments applied to artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons during continuous manufacturing before they are collected, specifically when the material is in staple-fibre form. It falls under mechanical methods for producing textiles or flexible materials not otherwise provided for, relating to the processing stage of artificial filament production.
[D01D 10/06] Washing or drying -- The D01D 10/06 entry covers washing or drying operations applied to artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons while they are still in a continuous manufacturing line, before collection. It falls under mechanical methods for making textiles or flexible materials not otherwise provided for, specifically physical treatment of the filaments during production.
[D01D 1/02] Preparation of spinning solutions -- The D01D 1/02 subclass covers methods and apparatus for preparing the liquid solutions or melts that serve as feedstock in the spinning of artificial filaments, threads, fibers, bristles or ribbons. It includes steps such as dissolving polymers, blending additives, and conditioning the solution to achieve suitable viscosity and homogeneity before extrusion.
[D01D 1/04] Melting filament-forming substances -- The code D01D 1/04 covers processes that melt filament-forming or similar substances before they are drawn into artificial fibres, threads, ribbons or bristles. It is part of the mechanical methods and apparatus subgroup for producing such textile materials, focusing on the heating step that brings the raw material to a molten state for subsequent filament formation.
[D01D 1/06] Feeding liquid to the spinning head -- The subclass D01D 1/06 concerns supplying liquid polymer or other filament-forming material to the spinning head in mechanical processes for producing artificial fibres, threads or ribbons. It includes designs for pumps, channels or other feeding mechanisms that deliver the material directly to the extrusion point.
[D01D 1/065] Addition and mixing of substances to the spinning solution or to the melt; Homogenising -- D01D 1/065 concerns the step in filament or fibre production where additives are introduced into the spinning solution or melt and the mixture is homogenised. It covers processes that mix or blend substances to modify the properties of the filament-forming material before it is drawn or solidified.
[D01D 1/09] Control of pressure, temperature or feeding rate -- D01D 1/09 covers the regulation of pressure, temperature or feed rate during mechanical processes that treat filament-forming or similar materials. It pertains to methods and apparatus used to control these parameters while producing artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons.
[D01D 1/10] Filtering or de-aerating the spinning solution or melt -- D01D 1/10 covers steps that remove particles or gases from the polymer solution or melt used in spinning artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons. The classification is placed under mechanical methods for treating filament-forming material, specifically filtering or de-aerating the spinning solution or melt in the textile manufacturing process.
[D01D 11/00] Other features of manufacture -- D01D 11/00 refers to auxiliary manufacturing steps or characteristics applied to artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons that are not covered by more specific subclasses. It includes processes such as drawing, heat-setting, surface treatment, coating or other finishing operations that modify the product's properties after its basic formation. This subclass captures any additional features of manufacture within the broader textile and flexible material category.
[D01D 11/02] Opening bundles to space the threads or filaments from one another -- This subclass covers processes and devices that separate a bundled group of artificial filaments, threads or fibres by opening the bundle to create individual spacing between them, typically as a preparatory step before further handling or weaving. It is used in textile manufacturing where precise spacing of filaments is required.
[D01D 1/103] De-aerating -- D01D 1/103 covers de-aerating processes applied to filament-forming or similar materials during their manufacture. The method removes entrapped air or gases from molten polymer or other filament precursors, typically by vacuum, gas displacement or mechanical means, to improve fibre quality and uniformity before extrusion or spinning.
[D01D 11/04] Fixed guides -- Fixed guides are components that keep a moving filament, thread, fibre or ribbon on a predetermined path during its mechanical manufacture, ensuring precise alignment and tension. They are typically stationary parts of apparatuses that direct the product through subsequent processing stages. This aids in consistent quality and dimensional control.
[D01D 1/106] Filtering -- D01D 1/106 relates to mechanical filtering operations applied to artificial filament-forming or similar materials during their manufacture. It covers methods and apparatus that cleanse, separate or remove unwanted particles from the filament, thread, fibre, bristle or ribbon as part of the treatment process.
[D01D 11/06] Coating with spinning solutions or melts -- D01D 11/06 covers processes in which artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons are coated during or after formation by applying a spinning solution or molten material, creating a surface layer that may enhance strength, elasticity, dyeability, protective qualities or other functional attributes.
[D01D 13/00] Complete machines for producing artificial threads -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Machines including both mechanical apparatus for forming fibres or filaments and mechanical apparatus for assembling the fibres or filaments into threads.
[D01D 13/02] Elements of machines in combination -- The subgroup D01D 13/02 covers combined elements of machinery used in complete machines for producing artificial threads, such as integrated drives, rollers, guides and other components that function together as a unit. It applies to textile equipment that manufactures synthetic filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons.
[D01D 4/00] Spinnerette packs -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Details about the constructional features and the cleaning of spinneret packs, i.e. the devices through which the polymer melt/solution is extruded  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Rotating spinnerets -> D01D5/18 - Spinnerets for making hollow filaments -> D01D5/24 - Spinnerets for making fibres with a non-round cross-section -> D01D5/253 - Spinnerets for making conjugated filaments -> D01D5/30 - Spinnerets for making hollow fibres membranes -> B01D69/085
[D01D 4/02] Spinnerettes -- D01D 4/02 covers spinnerette packs used in mechanical processes for producing artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons. It deals with the arrangement, mounting and replacement of spinnerettes in textile manufacturing equipment.
[D01D 4/022] Processes or materials for the preparation of spinnerettes -- D01D 4/022 covers processes and materials used to prepare spinnerette packs, the component of spinnerettes that holds the holes through which molten polymer is extruded to form artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons. The subclass pertains to mechanical methods for manufacturing these spinnerette assemblies in textile production.
[D01D 4/025] Melt-blowing or solution-blowing dies -- This CPC subclass covers dies used in melt-blowing or solution-blowing processes to form synthetic filaments, threads, or ribbons, where a molten or solution polymer is extruded through small orifices and attenuated by high-velocity gas streams. The dies are designed for producing non-woven fabrics and other flexible materials and are classified under D01D 4/025 in the textile manufacturing hierarchy.
[D01D 4/027] Spinnerettes containing inserts -- D01D 4/027 classifies spinnerettes that incorporate one or more inserts within the spinning head. The inserts may be used to modify filament geometry, cooling or tension during extrusion of synthetic fibres. This subclass falls under the broader group for mechanical methods and apparatus for producing artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons.
[D01D 4/04] Cleaning spinnerettes or other parts of the spinnerette packs -- This CPC subclass covers cleaning of spinnerettes and other components of spinnerette packs used in the mechanical manufacture of artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons. It includes methods and apparatus for removing residues, build-up or contamination from spinnerette plates, nozzles or related parts to maintain product quality.
[D01D 4/06] Distributing spinning solution or melt to spinning nozzles -- The D01D 4/06 subclass covers apparatus and methods for delivering a polymer solution or melt from a spinnerette pack to the individual spinning nozzles in filament production. It concerns the distribution system that ensures uniform flow to each nozzle during the mechanical manufacturing of artificial fibres, threads or ribbons.
[D01D 4/08] Supporting spinnerettes or other parts of spinnerette packs -- D01D 4/08 covers devices that support spinnerettes or any components of a spinnerette pack used in the mechanical production of synthetic filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons. The classification applies to apparatus that hold, align or otherwise assist spinnerettes during extrusion and drawing processes.
[D01D 5/00] Formation of filaments, threads, or the like -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Formation of filaments or the like  **Glossary:** - Simultaneous stretching: the stretching is done while the fibres are not yet solidified, i.e. before quenching or the like
[D01D 5/0007] Electro-spinning  non-woven fabrics produced by electro-spinning  D04H1/728
[D01D 5/0015] characterised by the initial state of the material -- The code covers mechanical processes or devices for producing artificial filaments, threads, fibers, bristles or ribbons where the starting condition of the raw material - such as being melt, solution, pre-spun, or solid - determines the method. It falls under textile manufacturing, specifically formation of filaments.
[D01D 5/0023] the material being a polymer melt -- This subclass covers processes for forming synthetic filaments, threads, fibres or ribbons when the feedstock is a polymer melt, focusing on the mechanical formation stage within textile manufacturing.
[D01D 5/003] the material being a polymer solution or dispersion  D01D5/0053  takes precedence -- D01D 5/003 is a CPC sub-group under the textile hierarchy concerning mechanical methods for forming artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons, specifically when the feedstock is a polymer solution or dispersion. It addresses processes that convert such liquid polymer media into solid filaments by extrusion, spinning or similar mechanical actions. Where a more detailed subclass such as D01D 5/0053 applies, it takes precedence over this broader entry.
[D01D 5/0038] the fibre formed by solvent evaporation, i.e. dry electro-spinning -- D01D 5/0038 covers the formation of filaments, threads or similar structures by dry electro-spinning, where a polymer solution is ejected from a nozzle, the solvent evaporates during flight, and a solid fibre is deposited. This method falls under mechanical techniques for producing artificial fibres within the textiles category of the Cooperative Patent Classification.
[D01D 5/0046] the fibre formed by coagulation, i.e. wet electro-spinning -- This subclass addresses fibers that are created by coagulation, specifically using wet electro-spinning where a polymer solution is extruded into a coagulating medium to form continuous filaments. It falls under mechanical methods for producing artificial filaments within the broader textiles and flexible materials category.
[D01D 5/0053] the material being a low molecular weight compound or an oligomer, and the fibres being formed by self-assembly -- This subclass covers processes where the feedstock is a low-molecular-weight compound or oligomer that spontaneously organizes into filaments, threads or ribbons without external shaping, relying on molecular self-assembly to form the fibers.
[D01D 5/0061] characterised by the electro-spinning apparatus -- D01D 5/0061 covers devices and arrangements specifically designed for producing filaments or fibers by electro-spinning, where a high-voltage electric field draws a polymer solution or melt into fine threads. The subclass falls within the broader category of mechanical methods for making artificial filaments in the textiles field.
[D01D 5/0069] characterised by the spinning section, e.g. capillary tube, protrusion or pin -- The subclass D01D 5/0069 covers apparatus for producing artificial filaments, threads or similar products where the defining feature lies in the spinning section of the machine. It includes designs that employ a capillary tube, a protrusion, a pin or comparable elements to shape and draw the material into continuous filaments. These elements control the extrusion and initial formation of the fibre.
[D01D 5/0076] characterised by the collecting device, e.g. drum, wheel, endless belt, plate or grid  D01D5/0046  takes precedence -- The subclass D01D 5/0076 relates to mechanical processes for producing artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons in which the filament is gathered on a rotating drum, wheel, endless belt, plate or grid after formation. It narrows the broader class for filament-forming apparatus and is superseded by subclass D01D 5/0046 when that more general feature applies.
[D01D 5/0084] Coating by electro-spinning, i.e. the electro-spun fibres are not removed from the collecting device but remain integral with it, e.g. coating of prostheses -- This CPC subclass covers methods that form a coating by electro-spinning where the spun fibres are left attached to the receiving device or substrate instead of being removed, such as applying a fibrous layer directly onto prosthetic implants. It falls under textile manufacturing, specifically mechanical processes for producing artificial filaments, threads or ribbons.
[D01D 5/0092] characterised by the electrical field, e.g. combined with a magnetic fields, using biased or alternating fields -- D01D 5/0092 relates to processes for forming synthetic filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons in which an electric field is applied, optionally together with a magnetic field, to influence material orientation or drawing; the field may be static (biased) or alternating. This subgroup falls under mechanical methods for producing artificial filaments within the broader textiles classification.
[D01D 5/02] Starting the formation -- D01D 5/02 covers the initial stage of producing artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons, where the basic filament material is first drawn, extruded or otherwise formed before subsequent processing. It falls under mechanical methods for textile manufacture in the CPC hierarchy, specifically within the broader categories of textiles, flexible materials and filament formation.
[D01D 5/04] Dry spinning methods -- The CPC subclass D01D 5/04 covers dry-spinning techniques used to form artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons. It pertains to mechanical processes that solidify a polymer solution or melt by evaporating a volatile solvent, producing continuous filaments without the use of a liquid coagulation bath.
[D01D 5/06] Wet spinning methods -- Wet spinning methods involve extruding a polymer solution or melt through spinnerets into a liquid coagulating bath, where the filament solidifies to form continuous fibers, threads, or ribbons. The technique is used for synthetic fibers such as rayon, acrylic and aramid and is classified under CPC D01D 5/06 within the mechanical methods for producing artificial filaments.
[D01D 5/08] Melt spinning methods -- D01D 5/08 covers melt-spinning techniques used to produce artificial filaments, threads, fibers, bristles or ribbons. The method involves heating a polymer to a molten state, extruding it through a spinneret, and solidifying the strand by cooling and drawing to achieve the desired dimensions and properties.
[D01D 5/082] of mixed yarn -- The D01D 5/82 subclass covers processes for producing mixed yarns, where two or more distinct filaments or threads are combined during formation to create a composite strand with differing material properties or colors, often used to achieve specific mechanical, aesthetic or functional characteristics.
[D01D 5/084] Heating filaments, threads or the like, leaving the spinnerettes -- The code D01D 5/084 covers processes in which filaments, threads or similar strands are heated after leaving the spinnerettes during their formation. The heating may be applied to set, dry, or improve the mechanical properties of the freshly extruded synthetic fibres. This falls under mechanical methods for making artificial filaments in the textile sector.
[D01D 5/088] Cooling filaments, threads or the like, leaving the spinnerettes -- The D01D 5/088 subclass covers mechanical techniques for cooling filaments, threads or similar products immediately after they leave the spinnerettes during artificial fibre production. It includes devices and methods that regulate temperature to solidify the material, improve dimensional stability and prepare the strand for further processing.
[D01D 5/0885] by means of a liquid -- This CPC subclass D01D 5/0885 covers processes that form artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons by means of a liquid, such as solution or suspension techniques. It falls under the mechanical methods for manufacturing textiles, specifically the formation step in the production of flexible material products.
[D01D 5/092] in shafts or chimneys -- The D01D 5/092 entry covers mechanical processes for producing artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons where the formation takes place within shafts or chimneys. It falls under the textile class for mechanical methods of manufacturing such filamentary products.
[D01D 5/096] Humidity control, or oiling, of filaments, threads or the like, leaving the spinnerettes -- This subclass covers processes that adjust moisture or apply lubricants to synthetic filaments, threads or ribbons as they exit the spinnerette during extrusion. It includes devices that humidify, dehumidify or oil the material to improve drawability, surface quality, or handling.
[D01D 5/098] with simultaneous stretching -- D01D 5/098 covers mechanical processes for producing artificial filaments, threads, fibres or ribbons in which the material is stretched at the same time as it is formed. The simultaneous stretching aligns the polymer molecules, improving tensile strength and dimensional stability of the final product.
[D01D 5/0985] by means of a flowing gas (e.g. melt-blowing) -- This CPC subclass covers processes and apparatus for forming artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons by passing a molten polymer stream into a flowing gas that draws it into fine continuous filaments, as employed in melt-blowing techniques.
[D01D 5/10] using organic materials -- D01D 5/10 covers mechanical processes for forming artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons that employ organic materials as the raw component. It falls under the textile hierarchy dealing with the manufacture of flexible materials not otherwise specified.
[D01D 5/11] Flash-spinning -- The code D01D 5/11 designates flash-spinning, a mechanical process in which a polymer melt or solution is forced through a small nozzle into a high-velocity gas stream, causing rapid solvent evaporation and immediate solidification into continuous filaments, threads, or similar textile fibres.
[D01D 5/12] Stretch-spinning methods -- The CPC subclass D01D 5/12 covers stretch-spinning methods for forming filaments, threads or similar textile elements by drawing the material while it is molten or semi-solid, producing elongated fibers with improved properties. It is part of the mechanical processes used in the manufacture of artificial filaments within the textiles hierarchy.
[D01D 5/14] with flowing liquid stretching media -- D01D 5/14 covers processes for producing artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons in which the material is stretched by a flowing liquid medium. The liquid stretches the extruded filament to orient the polymer and control diameter, often used in melt-spinning or solution-spinning operations. This sub-class falls under mechanical methods for filament formation within the textiles hierarchy.
[D01D 5/16] using rollers, or like mechanical devices, e.g. snubbing pins -- D01D 5/16 designates mechanical processes for shaping artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons that employ rollers or comparable devices such as snubbing pins. It belongs to the textiles hierarchy, under mechanical methods of producing synthetic filaments, and specifies the use of rotary or pin-type tooling to form and finish the material.
[D01D 5/18] by means of rotating spinnerets -- This subclass covers processes that produce synthetic filaments, threads or ribbons by using rotating spinnerets, where the spinneret spins to stretch the extruded material into continuous filaments. It is part of the CPC group for mechanical methods of manufacturing artificial fibres.
[D01D 5/20] with varying denier along their length -- D01D 5/20 covers methods and apparatus for producing artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons where the linear density (denier) changes along the length of the product. This includes processes that deliberately vary thickness or mass per unit length during spinning or drawing.
[D01D 5/22] with a crimped or curled structure -- This CPC subclass covers processes for producing synthetic filaments, threads, fibers, bristles or ribbons that acquire a crimped or curled shape during formation. The crimp may be introduced mechanically, thermally, chemically or via specially designed spinnerets, enhancing bulk, elasticity or texture of the final product.
[D01D 5/23] by asymmetrical cooling of filaments, threads, or the like, leaving the spinnerettes -- The subclass D01D 5/23 covers processes for making artificial filaments, threads or ribbons where the cooling of the filament after extrusion is deliberately uneven, creating a temperature gradient across the spinnerette. This asymmetrical cooling influences solidification, orientation or cross-sectional shape, allowing control of properties such as birefringence, strength or surface texture.
[D01D 5/24] with a hollow structure -- D01D 5/24 covers mechanical processes for forming artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons that possess a hollow interior. It includes methods such as extrusion or drawing that create a tube-like void within the filament, providing reduced weight or specialized functional characteristics.
[D01D 5/247] Discontinuous hollow structure or microporous structure -- This subclass covers methods and devices that generate artificial filaments, threads or ribbons possessing a discontinuous hollow or microporous internal architecture. Techniques may involve extrusion, drawing, or post-treatment steps that create segmented cavities or a network of pores within the fiber to provide properties such as enhanced breathability, filtration or light weight.
[D01D 5/253] with a non-circular cross section -- This CPC subclass relates to mechanical processes or equipment used to form artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons that have a non-circular cross-section. It falls under the broader group covering textile manufacturing methods for flexible materials not otherwise provided for.
[D01D 5/26] Formation of staple fibres -- The D01D 5/26 subclass of the CPC covers mechanical processes for producing staple (short) synthetic fibres, threads or ribbons. It includes methods such as extrusion, drawing, crimping, cutting or otherwise forming discontinuous filaments from polymer melts or solutions, forming the basic building blocks for textile yarns.
[D01D 5/28] while mixing different spinning solutions or melts during the spinning operation -- D01D 5/28 covers mechanical processes for forming synthetic filaments, threads or ribbons in which two or more distinct spinning solutions or melts are combined while the spinning takes place. The mixing occurs during the extrusion step, enabling blended or composite fibers to be produced in a single operation.
[D01D 5/30] Conjugate filaments -- The CPC subclass D01D 5/30 covers mechanical processes for producing conjugate filaments, which are composite or combined filaments that incorporate two or more distinct polymeric components in a single strand. It falls under the broader categories of textiles, flexible materials not otherwise provided for, and mechanical methods for making artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons, and specifies the formation step of such multi-component filaments.
[D01D 5/32] Side-by-side structure -- A side-by-side structure covers filaments or threads formed by extruding two or more polymer components adjacent to each other so that each material occupies a distinct longitudinal zone within the same filament. The arrangement yields combined mechanical or functional properties, such as varied stretch, moisture wicking, or surface texture, without mixing the materials at a molecular level. This subclass applies to production methods that create such multi-component, side-by-side yarns.
[D01D 5/34] Core-skin structure -- D01D 5/34 - Core-skin structure refers to a method of producing filaments, threads or ribbons where a central core material is surrounded by a different skin layer, often to combine properties such as strength and softness. This technique is used in textile manufacturing to create composite fibers with improved performance.
[D01D 5/36] Matrix structure -- The CPC subclass D01D 5/36 defines matrix structures produced in the mechanical formation of artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons. It addresses methods and apparatus that create a supporting matrix within the filament to enhance strength, stiffness or functional performance, and is nested under the textiles category for mechanical manufacturing processes.
[D01D 5/38] Formation of filaments, threads, or the like during polymerisation -- The D01D 5/38 subclass covers processes where filaments, threads, ribbons or similar products are formed directly during polymerisation, such as in-situ extrusion, spinning or drawing of the polymer melt or solution. It includes mechanical methods that create the continuous filament shape as the polymer chains polymerise.
[D01D 5/40] by applying a shearing force to a dispersion or solution of filament formable polymers, e.g. by stirring -- D01D 5/40 pertains to mechanical techniques for producing filaments, threads, fibres or similar by applying a shearing force to a dispersion or solution of filament-formable polymers, for example through stirring. This method falls under the textile manufacturing subclass dealing with formation of filaments.
[D01D 5/42] by cutting films into narrow ribbons or filaments or by fibrillation of films -- D01D 5/42 covers the mechanical formation of artificial filaments, threads or ribbons by cutting solid films into narrow strips or by fibrillating the films to produce fibre-like structures. The process is used for textiles and flexible materials where the filament is generated directly from a film substrate.
[D01D 5/423] by fibrillation of films or filaments -- The CPC subclass D01D 5/423 covers mechanical processes that produce artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons by fibrillating an existing film or filament, that is, by splitting or tearing the material into finer, separate filaments. This method is used in textile manufacturing to convert broader polymer films or thicker threads into finer, usable fibres.
[D01D 5/426] by cutting films -- This CPC subclass pertains to mechanical methods of producing artificial filaments, threads or similar textile elements by cutting a continuous film into separate strands. It falls within the hierarchy of textiles, flexible materials and manufacturing apparatus for artificial fibers.
[D01D 7/00] Collecting the newly-spun products -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Collecting the filaments or the like. Mechanical methods and apparatus for collecting fibres, filaments, yarns, threads or the like after spinning  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Electrospinning processes and apparatus characterized by the collector -> D01D5/0076 - Collection with simultaneous imparting of twist -> D01H
[D01D 7/02] in centrifugal spinning pots -- D01D 7/02 covers the step of collecting fresh fibers, filaments or ribbons directly from centrifugal spinning devices by means of spinning pots or similar receptacles. The subclass falls under mechanical methods for making artificial filaments, focusing on apparatus that gathers the newly-spun product as it exits the rotor.
[D01F] CHEMICAL FEATURES IN THE MANUFACTURE OF ARTIFICIAL FILAMENTS, THREADS, FIBRES, BRISTLES OR RIBBONS -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Chemistry-related aspects in the manufacture of artificial fibres, filaments and similar. It also covers - the chemical treatment of fibres and filaments during their production, e.g. before winding,  Apparatus specially adapted for the manufacture of carbon filaments is also covered.  **Glossary:** - Fibre: relatively short, elongated member of natural or artificial material - Filament: endless or quasi-endless, elongated member of natural or artificial material - Thread: assembly of yarns or filaments, usually produced by twisting - Yarn: unitary assembly of fibres, usually produced by spinning
[D01F 1/00] General methods for the manufacture of artificial filaments or the like -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Addition of additives to the spinning solution or melt.  D01F1/00 covers the chemical nature of the additive, whereas the method of adding the additive, that would be considered to be a mechanical feature, is classified in D01D1/065 .
[D01F 1/02] Addition of substances to the spinning solution or to the melt -- D01F 1/02 covers processes for manufacturing artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons in which a material-such as a dye, lubricant, stabiliser, polymer additive or other functional agent-is introduced into the spinning solution or melt before or during extrusion. The addition is intended to modify the properties of the filament, improve processing or impart specific functions to the finished product.
[D01F 1/04] Pigments -- D01F 1/04 Pigments relates to the incorporation of colourants into synthetic filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons during their production. It covers methods for adding organic, inorganic or composite pigments, dispersing them in the polymer matrix and treating the material to obtain the desired hue and performance.
[D01F 1/06] Dyes -- The D01F 1/06 subclass concerns dyes used in the production of artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons, focusing on chemical features that colour these synthetic textile materials during their manufacture. It includes general methods and compositions for applying colourants to such flexible materials.
[D01F 1/07] for making fire- or flame-proof filaments -- The CPC subclass D01F 1/07 covers processes for producing artificial filaments, threads, fibres or ribbons that are fire- or flame-proof, including the incorporation of flame-retardant agents or treatments applied during or after formation. It falls under chemical features in the manufacture of artificial filaments within the broader textiles hierarchy.
[D01F 1/08] for forming hollow filaments -- This subclass covers processes for forming hollow artificial filaments such as tubes or fibers with an internal lumen, used in textile applications. It includes extrusion, spinning, or other methods that create a hollow core during manufacture.
[D01F 1/09] for making electroconductive or anti-static filaments -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Also covers addition of additives to make antistatic fibres/filaments.
[D01F 1/10] Other agents for modifying properties -- D01F 1/10 covers auxiliary chemicals that are applied during the production of synthetic filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons to change their physical or functional properties. It includes agents such as plasticisers, antistatic compounds, lubricants, flame retardants and similar modifiers that are not covered by more specific subclasses.
[D01F 11/00] Chemical after-treatment of artificial filaments or the like during manufacture -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Chemical treatment of filaments and the like during their manufacture, i.e. during a continuous production process before the filaments have been collected.
[D01F 11/02] of cellulose, cellulose derivatives, or proteins -- This CPC subclass concerns post-manufacture chemical treatments applied to artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons where the treatment uses cellulose, its derivatives or protein-based substances, typically to modify surface properties, improve dye uptake, or enhance mechanical performance.
[D01F 1/103] Agents inhibiting growth of microorganisms -- D01F 1/103 covers chemical additives employed in the production of synthetic filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons that act as antimicrobial agents, preventing the growth of microorganisms on the material during manufacture or in the finished product. It is a sub-group of general methods for making artificial filaments.
[D01F 11/04] of synthetic polymers -- D01F 11/04 refers to chemical after-treatment of artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons made from synthetic polymers during manufacture, encompassing processes such as coating, bleaching, dyeing or other surface modifications to enhance material properties.
[D01F 1/106] Radiation shielding agents, e.g. absorbing, reflecting agents -- D01F 1/106 covers the use of radiation shielding agents such as absorbing or reflecting substances in the manufacture of artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons. The classification addresses additive components that protect against radiation during production or in the final product.
[D01F 11/06] of macromolecular compounds obtained by reactions only involving carbon-to-carbon unsaturated bonds -- This subclass covers post-manufacture chemical processes applied to synthetic fibers where the polymer is formed exclusively through carbon-carbon unsaturated bond reactions, such as diene polymerisation, and includes treatments that modify the filament after it is produced.
[D01F 11/08] of macromolecular compounds obtained otherwise than by reactions only involving carbon-to-carbon unsaturated bonds
[D01F 11/10] of carbon -- This subclass covers processes in which carbon is applied to artificial filaments, threads, fibres etc., as a post-treatment to impart properties such as conductivity, coloration, or surface modification. It includes methods of depositing carbon coatings, impregnation, or bonding carbonaceous substances onto the material during manufacturing.
[D01F 11/12] with inorganic substances -- This CPC subclass covers processes in which artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons are chemically after-treated using inorganic compounds during their manufacture. It includes steps such as applying, impregnating or coating the material with salts, oxides, acids, bases or other inorganic agents to confer properties like coloring, fire-retardance or strength. It falls under D01F 11/00 for chemical treatments of artificial filaments.
[D01F 11/121] Halogen, halogenic acids or their salts -- D01F 11/121 covers the use of halogen-containing compounds, halogenic acids or their salts as post-treatment chemicals applied to artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons during manufacturing. It belongs to the chemical-feature subclass for artificial filament production within the textiles hierarchy.

[D01F 11/124] Boron, borides, boron nitrides -- D01F 11/124 covers the use of boron, its borides and boron nitrides as chemical agents in after-treatment processes for artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons, typically to modify surface properties, improve durability or confer flame-resistance. This subclass falls under the broader group dealing with chemical features in the manufacture of textile-type flexible materials.
[D01F 11/125] Carbon -- The subclass D01F 11/125 covers the chemical after-treatment of artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons using carbon, such as carbon coating, doping or incorporation to modify the material's mechanical, electrical or thermal properties during manufacture.

[D01F 11/128] Nitrides, nitrogen carbides  nitrogen borides  D01F11/124 -- This subclass covers chemical after-treatment steps in the production of artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons that involve applying compounds containing nitrogen, such as nitrides, nitrogen carbides and nitrogen borides. Its focus is on the use of these nitrogen-based materials to modify surface or bulk properties of the synthetic textile product.
[D01F 11/129] Intercalated carbon- or graphite fibres -- The subclass D01F 11/129 covers chemical after-treatments applied to artificial filaments, threads or ribbons to produce intercalated carbon or graphite fibres, wherein additional substances are inserted between graphite layers to alter conductivity, strength or other performance characteristics. This process belongs to the textile and flexible-material field and relates to the manufacture of specialty synthetic fibres.
[D01F 11/14] with organic compounds, e.g. macromolecular compounds -- This subclass covers post-manufacture chemical treatment of artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons using organic substances, especially macromolecular compounds, to alter properties such as strength, dye uptake, elasticity or fire resistance. The process is applied during textile production to enhance the performance of synthetic fibres.
[D01F 11/16] by physicochemical methods -- D01F 11/16 covers the physicochemical after-treatment of artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons during their manufacture. The entry includes processes such as washing, heating, coating, cross-linking or other chemical modifications that improve the material's properties after it has been formed.
[D01F 13/00] Recovery of starting material, waste material or solvents during the manufacture of artificial filaments or the like -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Recovery of starting material, waste material or solvents during the manufacture of artificial filaments or the like.
[D01F 13/02] of cellulose, cellulose derivatives or proteins -- The D01F 13/02 subclass covers processes for recovering cellulose, its derivatives or protein-based starting materials, waste streams or solvents used in the production of artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons. It relates to chemical steps that retrieve and reuse these components during manufacture, reducing waste and improving material efficiency.

[D01F 2/00] Monocomponent artificial filaments or the like of cellulose or cellulose derivatives -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Artificial monocomponent fibres or the like of cellulose or its derivatives .
[D01F 2/02] from solutions of cellulose in acids, bases or salts -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Fibres spun from solutions of ionic liquids.
[D01F 2/04] from cuprammonium solutions -- D01F 2/04 covers the preparation of monocomponent artificial filaments, threads or fibres made from cellulose or its derivatives by dissolving the material in cuprammonium solutions and extruding the solution to form the filament.
[D01F 2/06] from viscose -- The CPC subclass D01F 2/06 covers the production of single-component artificial filaments made from cellulose or its derivatives that are obtained by the viscose process, including the steps of cellulose dissolution, treatment with alkali and carbon disulphide, extrusion and regeneration into filaments for textile use.
[D01F 2/08] Composition of the spinning solution or the bath -- The D01F 2/08 subclass concerns the formulation of the liquid medium used to spin single-component artificial filaments made from cellulose or its derivatives, describing the solvents, additives, and other chemical constituents of the spinning solution or bath.
[D01F 2/10] Addition to the spinning solution or spinning bath of substances which exert their effect equally well in either -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Addition of substances to the spinning solution or bath, these substances having an effect on the solution, on the bath or on the final fibre.
[D01F 2/12] Addition of delustering agents to the spinning solution -- The CPC subclass D01F 2/12 covers the addition of delustering agents to the spinning solution for producing monocomponent artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons made from cellulose or its derivatives. It is situated under chemical features in the manufacture of artificial fibres within the textiles hierarchy.
[D01F 2/14] Addition of pigments -- The D01F 2/14 subgroup covers methods for introducing pigments into monocomponent artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons made from cellulose or its derivatives. It relates specifically to the chemical step of adding colourants during the manufacture of these cellulose-based textile products.
[D01F 2/16] Addition of dyes to the spinning solution -- This subclass covers processes in which dyes are introduced into the spinning solution used to produce monocomponent artificial filaments made from cellulose or its derivatives. The addition of colourants during spinning enables the fibres to be dyed uniformly as they are formed, rather than requiring post-spinning treatment.
[D01F 2/18] Addition to the spinning solution of substances to influence ripening -- The D01F 2/18 entry covers the practice of introducing additives into the spinning solution for monocomponent artificial filaments made from cellulose or its derivatives, aiming to modify the ripening or setting behavior of the material during manufacture. This falls within chemical treatments applied to textiles and flexible synthetic fibres.
[D01F 2/20] for the manufacture of hollow threads -- D01F 2/20 covers processes used to produce hollow threads made from a single cellulose-based artificial filament, such as cellulose or its derivatives. The classification is situated in the textile section dealing with chemical features of artificial filament manufacture.
[D01F 2/22] by the dry spinning process -- The D01F 2/22 subclass covers monocomponent artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons made from cellulose or its derivatives that are produced using a dry-spinning process, where the polymer solution is extruded into a heated chamber and the solvent evaporates to solidify the filament. This falls under the broader categories of textiles, flexible materials, and chemical features in artificial filament manufacture.
[D01F 2/24] from cellulose derivatives -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Cellulose carbamate fibres.
[D01F 2/26] from nitrocellulose -- D01F 2/26 covers the production of monocomponent artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons made from cellulose or its derivatives when the raw material used is nitrocellulose. The classification pertains to the chemical steps involved in converting nitrocellulose into the finished filament product.
[D01F 2/28] from organic cellulose esters or ethers, e.g. cellulose acetate -- This subclass covers methods for producing single-component artificial filaments, threads or fibers made from cellulose derivatives by using organic cellulose esters or ethers such as cellulose acetate. It falls under chemical features in the manufacture of artificial filaments within the textile material hierarchy.
[D01F 2/30] by the dry spinning process -- Covers the production of single-component cellulose or cellulose-derivative artificial filaments by dry spinning, where a polymer solution is extruded into a heated medium and the solvent evaporates to solidify the filament.
[D01F 4/00] Monocomponent artificial filaments or the like of proteins -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Monocomponent fibres or the like of proteins.
[D01F 4/02] from fibroin -- D01F 4/02 refers to the production of artificial filaments, threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons that consist solely of a protein material, specifically fibroin, the silkworm protein. It covers the chemical steps for preparing monocomponent fibroin filaments used in textile applications.
[D01F 4/04] from casein -- D01F 4/04 covers the preparation of monocomponent artificial filaments in which casein, a milk-derived protein, is used as the sole raw material. The subclass includes processes for spinning, drawing and treating casein-based fibers, threads, bristles or ribbons for textile applications.
[D01F 4/06] from globulins, e.g. groundnut protein -- The CPC subclass D01F 4/06 relates to the manufacture of monocomponent artificial filaments made from protein globulins, for example groundnut protein. It covers processes that convert these protein sources into synthetic threads, fibres, bristles or ribbons used in textiles. The classification falls under chemical features in the manufacture of artificial fibres within the broader textiles hierarchy.

[D01F 9/12] Carbon filaments -- Carbon filaments are thin strands composed primarily of carbon, obtained by carbonising precursor fibres such as rayon or polyacrylonitrile and often coated or treated to improve conductivity and strength.
